kExcludeSelf };\\n75: \\n76: // Used in PaintLayerPaintOrderIterator.\\n77: enum PaintLayerIteration {\\n78:   kNegativeZOrderChildren = 1,\\n79:   // Normal flow children are not mandated by CSS 2.1 but are an artifact of\\n80:   // our implementation: we allocate PaintLayers for elements that\\n81:   // are not treated as stacking contexts and thus we need to walk them\\n82:   // during painting `invisible_for_position_visibility_`.\\n96: enum class LayerPositionVisibility : uint8_t {\\n97:   // anchors-visible, anchor intersection.\\n98:   kAnchorsIntersectionVisible = 1,\\n99:   // anchors-visible, anchor CSS visibility.\\n100:   kAnchorsCssVisible = 1 << 1,\\n101:   // anchors-visible, chained anchor visibility.\\n102:   kChainedAnchorsVisible = 1 << 2,\\n103:   // no-overflow.\\n104:   kNoOverflow = 1 << 3,\\n105: };\\n106: \\n107: // PaintLayer is an old object that handles lots of unrelated operations.\\n108: //\\n109: // We want it to die at some point and be replaced by more focused objects,\\n110: // which would remove (or at least compartmentalize) a lot of complexity.\\n111: // See the STATUS OF PAINTLAYER section below.\\n112: //\\n113: // The class is central to painting and hit-testing. That's because it handles\\n114: // a lot of tasks (we included ones done by associated satellite objects for\\n115: // historical reasons):\\n116: // - Complex painting operations (opacity, clipping, filters, reflections, ...).\\n117: // - hardware acceleration (through PaintLayerCompositor).\\n118: // - scrolling (through PaintLayerScrollableArea).\\n119: // - some performance optimizations.\\n120: //\\n121: // The compositing code is also based on PaintLayer. The entry to it is the\\n122: // PaintLayerCompositor, which fills |composited_layer_mapping| for hardware\\n123: // accelerated layers.\\n124: //\\n125: // TODO(jchaffraix): Expand the documentation about hardware acceleration.\\n126: //\\n127: //\\n128: // ***** SELF-PAINTING LAYER *****\\n129: // One important concept about PaintLayer is \\\"self-painting\\\"\\n130: // (is_self_painting_layer_).\\n131: // PaintLayer started as the implementation of a stacking context. This meant\\n132: // that we had to use PaintLayer's painting order (the code is now in\\n133: // PaintLayerPainter and PaintLayerStackingNode) instead of the LayoutObject's\\n134: // children order. Over the years, as more operations were handled by\\n135: // PaintLayer, some LayoutObjects that were not stacking context needed to have\\n136: // a PaintLayer for bookkeeping reasons. One such example is the overflow hidden\\n137: // case that wanted hardware acceleration and thus had to allocate a PaintLayer\\n138: // to get it. However overflow hidden is something LayoutObject can paint\\n139: // without a PaintLayer, which includes a lot of painting overhead. Thus the\\n140: // self-painting flag was introduced. The flag is a band-aid solution done for\\n141: // performance reason only. It just brush over the underlying problem, which is\\n142: // that its design doesn't match the system's requirements anymore.\\n143: //\\n144: // Note that the self-painting flag determines how we paint a LayoutObject:\\n145: // - If the flag is true, the LayoutObject is painted through its PaintLayer,\\n146: //   which is required to apply complex paint operations. The paint order is\\n147: //   handled by PaintLayerPainter::paintChildren, where we look at children\\n148: //   PaintLayers.\\n149: // - If the flag is false, the LayoutObject is painted like normal children (ie\\n150: //   as if it didn't have a PaintLayer). The paint order is handled by\\n151: //   BoxFragmentPainter.\\n152: // This means that the self-painting flag changes the painting order in a subtle\\n153: // way, which can potentially have visible consequences. Those bugs are called\\n154: // painting inversion as we invert the order of painting for 2 elements\\n155: // (painting one wrongly in front of the other).\\n156: // See https://crbug.com/370604 for an example.\\n157: //\\n158: //\\n159: // ***** STATUS OF PAINTLAYER *****\\n160: // We would like to remove this class in the future. The reasons for the removal\\n161: // are:\\n162: // - it has been a dumping ground for features for too long.\\n163: // - it is the wrong level of abstraction, bearing no correspondence to any CSS\\n164: //   concept.\\n165: //\\n166: // Its features need to be migrated to helper objects. This was started with the\\n167: // introduction of satellite objects: PaintLayer*. Those helper objects then\\n168: // need to be moved to the appropriate LayoutObject class, probably to a rare\\n169: // data field to avoid growing all the LayoutObjects.\\n170: //\\n171: // A good example of this is PaintLayerScrollableArea, which can only happen\\n172: // be instanciated for LayoutBoxes. class FilterOperations;\n70: class HitTestResult;\n71: class HitTestingTransformState;\n72: class PaintLayerScrollableArea;\n73: \n74: enum IncludeSelfOrNot { kIncludeSelf, kExcludeSelf };\n75: \n76: // Used in PaintLayerPaintOrderIterator.\n77: enum PaintLayerIteration {\n78:   kNegativeZOrderChildren = 1,\n79:   // Normal flow children are not mandated by CSS 2.1 but are an artifact of\n80:   // our implementation: we allocate PaintLayers for elements that\n81:   // are not treated as stacking contexts and thus we need to walk them\n82:   // during painting and hit-testing.\n83:   kNormalFlowChildren = 1 << 1,\n84:   kPositiveZOrderChildren = 1 << 2,\n85: \n86:   kStackedChildren = kNegativeZOrderChildren | kPositiveZOrderChildren,\n87:   kNormalFlowAndPositiveZOrderChildren =\n88:       kNormalFlowChildren | kPositiveZOrderChildren,\n89:   kAllChildren =\n90:       kNegativeZOrderChildren | kNormalFlowChildren | kPositiveZOrderChildren\n91: };\n92: \n93: // TODO(crbug.com/332933527): Support anchors-valid.\n94: // If the size of this enum changes, make sure to update the bits needed for\n95: // `invisible_for_position_visibility_`.\n96: enum class LayerPositionVisibility : uint8_t {\n97:   // anchors-visible, anchor intersection.\n98:   kAnchorsIntersectionVisible = 1,\n99:   // anchors-visible, anchor CSS visibility.\n100:   kAnchorsCssVisible = 1 << 1,\n101:   // anchors-visible, chained anchor visibility.\n102:   kChainedAnchorsVisible = 1 << 2,\n103:   // no-overflow.\n104:   kNoOverflow = 1 << 3,\n105: };\n106: \n107: // PaintLayer is an old object that handles lots of unrelated operations.\n108: //\n109: // We want it to die at some point and be replaced by more focused objects,\n110: // which would remove (or at least compartmentalize) a lot of complexity.\n111: // See the STATUS OF PAINTLAYER section below.\n112: //\n113: // The class is central to painting and hit-testing. That's because it handles\n114: // a lot of tasks (we included ones done by associated satellite objects for\n115: // historical reasons):\n116: // - Complex painting operations (opacity, clipping, filters, reflections, ...).\n117: // - hardware acceleration (through PaintLayerCompositor).\n118: // - scrolling (through PaintLayerScrollableArea).\n119: // - some performance optimizations.\n120: //\n121: // The compositing code is also based on PaintLayer. The entry to it is the\n122: // PaintLayerCompositor, which fills |composited_layer_mapping| for hardware\n123: // accelerated layers.\n124: //\n125: // TODO(jchaffraix): Expand the documentation about hardware acceleration.\n126: //\n127: //\n128: // ***** SELF-PAINTING LAYER *****\n129: // One important concept about PaintLayer is \"self-painting\"\n130: // (is_self_painting_layer_).\n131: // PaintLayer started as the implementation of a stacking context. This meant\n132: // that we had to use PaintLayer's painting order (the code is now in\n133: // PaintLayerPainter and PaintLayerStackingNode) instead of the LayoutObject's\n134: // children order. Over the years, as more operations were handled by\n135: // PaintLayer, some LayoutObjects that were not stacking context needed to have\n136: // a PaintLayer for bookkeeping reasons. One such example is the overflow hidden\n137: // case that wanted hardware acceleration and thus had to allocate a PaintLayer\n138: // to get it. However overflow hidden is something LayoutObject can paint\n139: // without a PaintLayer, which includes a lot of painting overhead. Thus the\n140: // self-painting flag was introduced. The flag is a band-aid solution done for\n141: // performance reason only. It just brush over the underlying problem, which is\n142: // that its design doesn't match the system's requirements anymore.\n143: //\n144: // Note that the self-painting flag determines how we paint a LayoutObject:\n145: // - If the flag is true, the LayoutObject is painted through its PaintLayer,\n146: //   which is required to apply complex paint operations. The paint order is\n147: //   handled by PaintLayerPainter::paintChildren, where we look at children\n148: //   PaintLayers.\n149: // - If the flag is false, the LayoutObject is painted like normal children (ie\n150: //   as if it didn't have a PaintLayer). The paint order is handled by\n151: //   BoxFragmentPainter.\n152: // This means that the self-painting flag changes the painting order in a subtle\n153: // way, which can potentially have visible consequences. Those bugs are called\n154: // painting inversion as we invert the order of painting for 2 elements\n155: // (painting one wrongly in front of the other).\n156: // See https://crbug.com/370604 for an example.\n157: //\n158: //\n159: // ***** STATUS OF PAINTLAYER *****\n160: // We would like to remove this class in the future. The reasons for the removal\n161: // are:\n162: // - it has been a dumping ground for features for too long.\n163: // - it is the wrong level of abstraction, bearing no correspondence to any CSS\n164: //   concept.\n165: //\n166: // Its features need to be migrated to helper objects. This was started with the\n167: // introduction of satellite objects: PaintLayer*. Those helper objects then\n168: // need to be moved to the appropriate LayoutObject class, probably to a rare\n169: // data field to avoid growing all the LayoutObjects.\n170: //\n171: // A good example of this is PaintLayerScrollableArea, which can only happen\n172: // be instanciated for LayoutBoxes. With the current design, it's hard to know\n173: // that by reading the code.\n174: class CORE_EXPORT PaintLayer : public GarbageCollected<PaintLayer>,\n175:                                public DisplayItemClient {\n176:  public:\n177:   explicit PaintLayer(LayoutBoxModelObject*);\n178:   PaintLayer(const PaintLayer&) = delete;\n179:   PaintLayer& operator=(const PaintLayer&) = delete;\n180:   ~PaintLayer() override;\n181: \n182:   void Destroy();\n183: \n184:   // DisplayItemClient methods\n185:   String DebugName() const final;\n186:   DOMNodeId OwnerNodeId() const final;\n187: \n188:   LayoutBoxModelObject& GetLayoutObject() const { return *layout_object_; }\n189:   LayoutBox* GetLayoutBox() const {\n190:     return DynamicTo<LayoutBox>(layout_object_.Get());\n191:   }\n192:   // Returns |GetLayoutBox()| if it exists and has fragments.\n193:   const LayoutBox* GetLayoutBoxWithBlockFragments() const;\n194: \n195:   PaintLayer* Parent() const { return parent_.Get(); }\n196:   PaintLayer* PreviousSibling() const { return previous_.Get(); }\n197:   PaintLayer* NextSibling() const { return next_.Get(); }\n198:   PaintLayer* FirstChild() const { return first_.Get(); }\n199:   PaintLayer* LastChild() const { return last_.Get(); }\n200: \n201: ","url":"https://sourcegraph.sourcegraph.com/github.com/sg-evals/chromium--2d05e315@524690a4542d3d93020fb4764b8ba5cc968d1a3d/-/blob/third_party/blink/renderer/core/paint/paint_layer.h%3FL1-200"}}}

It groups one or more LayoutObjects that paint together. PaintLayers are crucial for implementing complex painting operations (opacity, clipping, filters, reflections), hardware acceleration through compositing, scrolling, and performance optimizations. Not all LayoutObjects have a corresponding PaintLayer - only those that require special treatment for painting purposes.\\n\\n4. **Display List Recording (PaintController + DisplayItemList)** - Files: third_party/blink/renderer/platform/graphics/paint/paint_controller.h and third_party/blink/renderer/platform/graphics/paint/display_item_list.h\\n   - PaintController (defined at line 131 in paint_controller.h) is responsible for processing display items as they are produced and creating a final paint artifact when complete. It includes logic for caching, cache invalidation, and merging of paint operations.\\n   - DisplayItemList (defined at line 28 in display_item_list.h) is a container for a list of display items of various types. It stores the actual paint operations that will be rasterized to pixels.\\n\\nThe flow progresses: Style (CSS) → Layout (geometry) → Paint Layers (grouping) → Display Items (recording paint operations) → Rasterization. When a CSS style changes, the StyleResolver recomputes styles, which triggers layout recalculation, layer updates, and finally display item recording for the affected elements.\"\n}\n","structuredPatch":[],"originalFile":null}}
